DOMINICAN REPUBLIC
FIFTH ROAD REHABILITATION AND MAINTENANCE PROJECT
Terms of Reference for Technical Assistance for SEOPC
in Road Maintenance Management
Obiectives
1.         The objective of this technical assistance will be *o develop a
comprehensive national road maJntenance program along lines pL .osed by DGM
and SEOPC.
Background
2.       From 1976 to 1979, Loan 1316-DO provided funds for the design of a
maintenance management system. From 1980 to 1982, under Loan 1709-DO, a
new technical assistince by consultants simplified and adapted the system
to the specific needs of the country. Standards for routine maintenance
works were developed and engineers, foremen and workers were trained as
needed. The system was never implemented. The planning criteria proposed
in the system have been used as starting point for preparing the
maintenance programs included in the on-going road project supported by
the World Bank. However, the system should be updated and implemented on a
consistent basis in the central office and in the districts.
Scope of the Assistance
3.       The principal tasks to be performed by this technical assistance
are the following:
(a) Reviewing, updating and adapting the existing system or
proposing an alternative system;
(b) revising the available data and collecting the inputs
required to implement the system;
(c) implementing a maintenance management system;
(d) implementing an equipment management system;
(e) implementing a computerized analysis of the systems;
(f) applying cost accounting to road maintenance;
(g) preparing a three-year national maintenance program and its
budget (1994-1996) using the implemented systems;
(h) formulating a program (l194-96) for maintenance by contract;
and,
(i) personnel training.
4.       The first task will consist of reviewing the adaptability of
existing maintenance management systems (the present DGM system and those
of other road institutions in Latin America) to the conditions in the
Dominican Republic. After this analysis, the consultant will propose to



ANNEX 7
- 113 -                  Page 2 of 4
SEOPC the system to be implemented. Upon SEOPC approval of the proposal,
the consultant will set up the selected system. In this phase the
consultant will determine maintenance activities, quantity of works,
maintenance levels, performance standards and the unit costs to be used in
the system.
5.       The second task will include the programs for collecting road
roughness data (using the Mays Road Meter) and deflections (with the
Falling Weight Deflectometer). This task will also include identification,
evaluation and selection of sources of appropriate materials for road
maintenance, including the analysis of problems concerning development of
borrow pits and transportation of materials.
6.       The third task, (implementation of the maintenance management
system) will be strengthening DGM's technical and administrative
capabilities, setting up the procedures for planning, budgeting and
monitoring highway maintenance programs. The system will be implemented at
the central level and in the districts, considering routine and periodic
maintenance and minor improvements. The system will allow to organize the
districts and Oayudantias* to carry out the road maintenance programs.
These maintenance programs will be prepared starting with the needs of the
layudantias* and then, obtaining the program of the districts as a sum of
the programs of the Oayudantias', and the national program as a sum of the
programs of the districts. The implementation of the system at the
district level will allow the districts to prepare and monitor its monthly
road maintenance programs.
7.       The fourth task will be to study and imolement an equipment
management system. First, the consultant will collect and analyze the data
on the availability and use of SEOPC's equipment fleet. He will also: i)
analyze the outputs and operating cost of DGM's equipment and will update
the existing equipment inventory; ii) evaluate current DGM's programs &nd
policies on equipment management, preventive maintenance levels and DGW's
workshops management; iii) analyze the procedures in equipment control
including forms and reports currently used; iv) evaluate the procedures
used to obtain equipment operating and maintenance costs;   v) analyze and
evaluate the control procedures for spare parts including stocks and
inventories; and, vi) recommend the policies and procedures to be followed
in the future.
8.       The fifth task will be the implementation of computerized analysis
of the management systems. The consultant will prepare and implement:
i) computerized programs for planning, budgeting and monitoring the road
and equipment maintenance programs; and, ii) analysis and assessment of
maintenance policies using mathematical models for short, medium and long
term.
9.       The sixth task will be the application of cost accounting to road
maintenance. The main objective of this task is setting up a cost
accountability system to support the maintenance and equipment management
system and introducing reliable procedures to monitor SEOPC's payments and
expenditures according to work progress.



ANNEX 7
- 114 -                  Page S of 4
10.      The seventh task will be the preparation of a detailed national
maintenance program and its budget for the period 1994-1996. This program
will be prepared based on the previously implemented maintenance, equipment
and computer systems. It will be initiated in the last pbase of the
technical assistance and include assistance to SEOPC by the consultant in
implementing the program and preparing the appropriate documents for
government approval.
11.      The eighth task will be the formulation of a program to carry out
maintenance by contract in the period 1994-1996. The consultants, will
select the works to be contracted starting from the maintenance program for
this period and will prepare bidding documents for the procurement of
contractor services. They will also group the works in lots whose size
will be attractive to local contractors, in function of their equipment and
working capital.
12.      The ninth task will be personnel training.  The consultant will:
i) assess the SEOPC's current policies and minimum needs in training
specialists; ii) assess and update the personnel directly involved in
maintenance activities, in the central office, in the districts and in the
"ayudantias', by category; iii) prepare and carry out a training plan for
technical and administrative personnel involved in maintenance planning,
execution and control; iv) set up a system of evaluation and control of the
training programs; and, v) prepare a study of DGH's personnel needs at the
central office and in the districts for the period 1994-96, based on the
maintenance programs for this period.
Staffing
13.      The technical assistance will be provided by the following
specialists:
i)   A highway engineer, with experience in maintenance and
equipment management systems, maintenance by contract and
maintenance planning and budgeting, who will be the program
leader and coordinator. (24 months)
ii) An equipment specialist, with experience in equipment
management systems. (18 months)
iii) A computer system analyst. (12 months)
iv) An specialist in maintenance cost accounting. (9 months)
v)   A personnel training specialist. (12 months)
14.      It is envisaged that this technical assistance will be carried out
over a period of two years and will require a total of 75 man-months. All
staff must be fluent in Spanish.
Executing Government Agency and Counterpart Staff
15.      DGM will be the technical assistance executing agency.  The
counterpart staff will be selected by SEOPC from DGH permanent staff at the
central office and at the districts.



ANNEX 7
- 115 -                  Page 4 of 4
Schedule and Reports
16.      By the first month, the consultants will submit an initial
program with the activities to be carried out in the time period
established by the contract (24 months). This program will consist of, but
not necessarily be limited to, the followings
i)   analysis and evaluation of the existing situation;
ii) implementation of the technical assistance in accordance with
the initial program approved by DGM;
iii) monitoring of the maintenance programs for 1992-93 and
preparation of the maintenance programs and budgets for
1994-96; and,
iv) monitoring of the systems implemented.
17.      In addition to the initial program, the consultant will submit
quarterly reports to the DGM Director General, during the period in which
services are rendered, and a final repor; by the end of the contract, which
already include SEOPC's comments and suggestions.

DOMINICAN REPUBLIC
FIFTH ROAD REHABILITATION AND MAINTENANCE PROJECT
TERMS OF REFEIENCE FOR A STUDY OF THE CONSTRUCTION IDUSTRY
1. Objectives
The objective of this study is to identify the main constraints
and o1stacles preventing the domestic construction industry of the
Dominican Republic from assuming a more effective role in the country's
construction and maintenance programs and to develop appropriate detailed
plans of action to overcome those constraints.
The work process should be to undertake a brief but balanced and
careful overview, and then to focus on the main issues on which action is
needed. Most of the effort of the study will, thus, be devoted to
identifying and considering alternative, viable solutions to the problems
and to working up action plans for their implementation.
To ensure full commitment of the government and of the industry to
the execution of the strategy and action plans, they should be developed in
close collaboration with the Secretariat of Public Works (SEOPC), acting
liaison agency for the study team, and with the construction industry's
representatives and professional associations.
2. Scope of the Study
The study of the construction industry in the Dominican Republic,
and the formulation of a strategy and action plans will be based on a
careful consideration of the following subjects:
2.1  Structure of the Industry
(a)   Historical development of the industry including emergence of
entrepreneurs and ownership characteristics of construction
enterprises.
(b)   Participation of the industry in the economy of the country
'ncluding contribution to employment, backward and forward
linkages, particularly with the construction materials
industry, and comparison with developed countries and with
countries at a similar stage of development.



- 117.-
Annex 8
Page 2 of 6
(c)   Participation of the main sectors of the industry in the
satisfaction of the overall demand for construction and
maintenance services; historical participation, and future
trends.
(d)   Experience with joint ventures and domestic sub-contractors
of foreign firms.
2.2  Demand
(a)   Overall demand:  historical series, fluctuation of annual
growth rates relative to the manufacturing industry and GDP,
and identification of trends.
(b)   Forecast future demand, identifying, in particular:
(i)   Recurring demand for construction and maintenance
services which can potentially be supplied by the
domestic private sector;
(i)   Recurring demand for construction and maintenance
services which would preferably be catered for by force
account operations; and
(iii)  Demand for larger construction works which can be
handled by domestic enterprises, either by slicing and
packaging or by providing those enterprises with
technical and financial assistance.
2.3  Procurement and Contract Administration
(a)   Procedures for procurement in the public and private sectors;
regulations for bidding and negotiating construction and
maintenance work; existence and adequacy of contractor's
registry; time consumed and difficulties encountered in the
post-bid process, up to the start of work.
(b)   contract forms and contracting practice; fairness of contract
provisions, particularly in the apportionment of risk between
owner and contractor; compensation to the contractor for
default by the owner (for example interest payable for late
progress payments, or compensation for delays induced by the
owner); adequacy of provisions for price escalation and
settlement of disputes; existence of indices or data sources
for applying escalation provisions.



- 118 -
Annex 8
Page 3 of 6
(c)   Policy and legal framework for contracting with public sector
construction organizations.
(d)   Adequacy of owner's establishment to manage contracts and
supervise construction; autonomy of government supervisors;
adequacy of consultants employed for supervision;
restrictions which may inhibit the engagement of competent
supervisors.
(el  Adequacy of the engineering process to the level of
development of the domestic construction industry.
(f)   Anomalies and difficulties observed in the process of
procurement, management, and completion of construction
contracts.
2.4 Choice of Technology
(a)   Potential for the employment of alternative technologies in
construction.
(b)   pricing distortions which may influence choice against
locally available, traditional construction materials.
2.5  The Industry
(a)   Level of development of civil construction sectors, according
to specified indicators of complexity and volume of the
operations the domestic enterprises can handle.
(b)   Ownership and organization of construction enterprises state
and private, and problems and constraints of each, in
particular efficiency of each type of organization.
(c)   Entrepreneurs and managers:  their status in society;
potential supply of entrepreneurs and managers; traditional
attitudes; willingness of leaders to learn modern management
techniques; facilities available for coaching entrepreneurs
and managers; salary levels.
(d)   Supply of engineers, architects, estimators, surveyors,
accountants, senior clerks, foremen, and other middle-level
managers; traditional sources, adequacy of supply, and
training facilities available; salary levels.



- 3119 -
Annex 
Page 4 of 6
(e)   Supply of equipment operators and mechanics; adequacy of
supply and training facilities available; proficiency levels
relative to the quality of finished work; wage levels.
(f)   Adequacy of salary and wage regimes for state and private
construction enterprises; problems arising from these
regimes.
(g)   Labor productivity and feasible incentives.
(h)   Equipment resources:  restrictions for the importation and
ownership of construction equipment; standardization;
availability of spare parts and servicing facilities;
restrictions on the importation of spare parts; availability
of excess equipment in government fleets which could be sold
or hired out to contracting enterprises; prices of
consumables.
(i)   Availability of materials:  shortages which affect
construction; alternatives available; means of marketing and
distribution, accessibility of self-help builders; prices of
domestic and imported materials.
(j)   Technology gaps in estimating, planning, organizing and
managing construction work, cost control, and construction
technology; quality of finished work.
(k)   Research and development facilities available for the
industry; identification of needs.
2.6  Financing
(a)   Financing, bonding, guarantee and insurance requirements of
builders and civil contractors.
(b)   Perception of the industry by domestic financiers, bondsmen,
and insurers. Financial indicators wbich confirm or do not
confirm this perception.
(c)   Particular characteristics of construction risk in the
Dominican Republic.
(d)   Availability of credit for the industry from commercial
banks, DFCs, nonbanking sources, suppliers' credit. Terms
and conditions on which credit, bonds. and guarantees are
advanced to the industry. Capability of the industry to meet
those terms and conditions.



- 120 -
Annex a
Page Sof 6
(e)   Availability of suitable insurance facilitSes; other forms of
ii.surance required In contracting.
(f)   Suitability of contractual arrp-gements (advances or progress
payments) in the context of the financial resources available
to the industry. Acceptance by financiers of government
progress certificates and other contractual documents for
discounting. Terms of such discounting.
2.7 Legal
(a)   Taxation regime applicable to the construction industry.  Tax
exemptions and concessions (particularly, incentives for re-
investment), depreciation allowances. protection of industry
against foreign competition. Pricing and profit controls.
(b)   Employment regime.  Permanence of labor in construction
industry employment. Wage-fixing procedures, free
bargaining.  Social laws (health, insurance, pension, and so
forth) applicable to construction. Methods available for
settlement of disputes. History or periodicity of disputes.
(c)   Importation regime.  Duties or quotas levied on equipment,
spare parts, and materials. Treatment of domestic and
foreign companies. Restriction in the availability of
foreign currency.
(d)   Company and ownership laws applicable to the industry.
(e)   Codes and regulations affecting the industry (for instance,
licensing of contractors, determination and limitations of
responsibility, building codes, safety and fire regulations).
2.8 Institutional
(a)   Existence of a government office responsible for development
of the industry and for liaising with industry institutions.
(b)   Existence of an institution representat..ve of the industry,
capable of presenting its views to the government in matters
affecting construction and providing management information
and training services to construction enterprises.
(c)   Existence of professional associations related to the
construction activity (for engineers and architects, for
example).



- 121 -
Annex 8
Page 6 of 6
3. Strategy and Action Plens
A comprehensive strategy for development of the industry will be
prepared, to enhance the level of development of the industry. The
strategy will propose short-, medium, and long-term objectives. These
shall take into account the state of development of the country's economy
and its likely evolution when proposing a time frame.
A small number of action plans, aimed at resolving key problems
and constraints identified in the strategy as having a high priority will
be prepared. The plans will contain schedules and programs for their
implementation, the persons or institutions responsible, the estimated
costs and likely sources of funding, and the standards by which to appraise
the results of these programs.
4. Study Team. Program
Two professionals for a total of 8 months.

- 122 -                    Page i of 4
DOMINICAN REPUBLIC
FIFTH ROAD REHABILITATION AND MAINTENANCE PROJECT
SANTO DOMINGO URBAN TRANSPORT STUDY-TERMS OF REFERENCE
I. Oblectives
Objectives of the study are to:
(a) improve the accessibility, quality of service, operational
efficiency, and costs of public transport, and encourage
private sector participation;
(b) preserve transport infrastructure investments and reduce
accidents, delays and vehicle operating costs through
implementation of coordinated traffic management actions; and
(c) strengthen institutional capability, at the local as well as
national level, to provide effective policy development,
planning resource allocation, traffic system implementation
and operation, and project replicability.
II. Scope of Work
-ask A:  Subsector Analysis
The purpose of this task is to provide an overview of existing
conditions in the subsector and thereby establish a factual basis for
recommendations developed in subsequent tasks. The consultant shall use
the criteria defined in Attachment A in the development of this analysis.
Task B: Traffic Management
Prepare a program of relatively low-cost traffic management
improvement which can be implemented quickly within existing rights-of-way
to improve the flow of traffic, particularly buses, on major corridors and
at critical intersections.
B.1 - Traffic Signals - Based on the existing program of the
Municipality of Santo Domingo, and information in Task A, identify needed
improvements to existing traffic signalization including hardware and
related improvements in operations and maintenance. This will involve
approximately 120 intersections. Develop cost estimates, benefits, and
performance specifications for subsequent procurem:nt of equipment and
installation.
B.2 - Intersection Improvement - Based on data developed in the
subsector analysis and in conjunction with recommended traffic signal
improvements, prepare recommendations, at the level of preliminary
engineering design, for operational and geometric improvements at the ten
most critical intersections. Estimate cost and benefits of this program.



ANNEX 9
-123 -                      Page 2 of 4
B.3 - Si$ns and Markings - Based on the program of the
Municipality and in conjunction with the results of Tasks B.1 and B.2,
recommend a program for the improvement of signs and markings in the
metropolitan area including recommendations for installation and
maintenance.
Task C: Traffic Safety and Enforcement
The purpose of this task is to improve the enf,roement of traffic
regulations, improve accident investigation and record-keeping, and
facilitate coordination among the agencies involved.
C.1 - Accident Records Management - Develop recommendations for
improvement in accident records management, including terms of reference
for training in accident investigation and reporting procedures. Develop
recommendations for data format and storage. Propose measures for periodic
analysis and coordination among public agencies that may share
responsibility for countermeasures.
C.2 - Police Equipment and Technical Assistance - Review the
current level of traffic law enforcement and identify the need for
additional equipment such as vehicles, radios, tow trucks, etc., to improve
the level of enforcement. Develop terms of reference for technical
assistance, if necessary, to help the police improve enforcement through
training and public awareness campaigns.
Task D: Urban Road Maintenance
The purpose of this task is to develop a five-year maintenance and
rehabilitation program for the rimary urban road network; and prepare
terms of reference for development, during the project, of a Maintenance
Management System which can be used by the responsible agency to plan and
carry out a cost-effective maintenance and rehabilitation plan for the
entire roadway system.
D.1 - Physical Inventory of Primary System - Based on data
develeped in Task A, conduct a field survey for the existing primary
network. For each section of road identifys
-    general geometric and physical characteristics such as
length, pavement width, type of pavement surface, and year of
application (if known);
-    presence and average height of curbs;
-    presence and type of construction of sidewalks;
-    type of drainage facilities.
D.2 - Condition Analysis - By visual inspection, note pavement
condition and specific types of failures, estimate pavement roughness in
cm/km, and make an approximate assessment of the adequacy of base, subbase,
and drainage facilities.



ANNEX 9,
- 124-                     Page 3 of 4
D.3 - Recommended Work Protram - Using data developed In Tasks A,
D.1 and D.2 develop a five-year program for routine and periodic
maintenance, and roadway rehabilitation, for the primary network. Evaluate
the economic benefits of such program.
Task E: Public Transport
The purpose of this task is to develop demand projections and
recommend policy actions to increase efficiency and level of supply of
existing passenger services.
E.1 - Demand Proiection and Required SupylY - Based on the data
collected in task A, project future (ten-year horizon) urban passonger
flows along major routes. Calculate likely requirement for vehicles for
this demand level.
E.2 - Role of Private Sector - Recommend Government actions
required to assist the private sector in providing urban passengers with
the required services. The areas covered here should include import
policies, taxations, level and structure of fares, assignment of routes and
frequencies and licensing policies. Particular attention should be given
to defining the role of non-bus passenger transport.
E.3 - Public Sector Bus Company - define the role of the public
bus company (ONATRATE) and recommend means to restore its financial
viability.
Task F: Institutional Development
The purpose of this task is to examine the existing structure for
managing the urban transport system.
P.1 - Organization - Based on the information gathered in the
above tasks, prepare recommendations for necessary improvement to the
institutional framework for urban transport, including specific
recommendations in the following areas:
-    division of responsibility among agencies (both functional
and geographical);
-    changes in existing statutes, regulations and policies;
-    for each affected agency, the internal structure necessary to
achieve its mission;
-    provisions for necessary interagency linkages and
coordination in preparation of programs and budgets, physical
planning, scheduling, execution and supervision;
F.2 - Human Resources Development - Based on the institutional
reforms and work programs recommended in the above tasks, propose a
parallel program of human resource development for each affected agency,
including the number, types ard qualifications of additional personnel in
each job category. Provide job descriptions for new or redesigned
positions.



ANNEX 9
- 125 -                    Page 4 of 4
III. Time and Reporting Schedule
The consultant shall begin work within 30 days of the contract
becoming effective. The consultant shall prepare and submit to the
government the following reports, in Spanish, within the time peliods
indicated.
(a) Quarterly progress reports giving a summary of the work
performed during the reporting period, and outline of the
work scheduled for the next reporting period, and indicating
the percentage of completion of the work under each major
task and subtask in the Terms of Reference.
(b) A draft final report summarizing all work performed during
the study and the findings and recommendations of the
consultants, within nine (9) months of the starting date.
(c) A final report incorporating all revisions deemed appropriate
by the consultants after comments on the draft final report
by the Government and the Bank, within 30 days after receipt
of all comments.
The draft final and final report shall contain a concise first
chapter summarizing all major findings and recommendations of the
consultants. The calculations of costs and benefits and all economic
analysis which support the consultants' conclusions shall be made available
in sufficient detail to permit checking of all calculations without
supplementary data.
IV. Level of Effort
It is anticipated that the herein described tachnical assistance
will require approximately twenty four (24) man-months of professional
level staff and fourteen (14) man-months of technical level staff.
Consultants should regard this only as indicative and are free to propose
whatever staffing they consider appropriate.

URBAN TRANSPORT ANALYSIS
Traffic Management
1.       Network Characteristics:  from existing data, prepare plans for
the metropolitan area showing:
(M)    the present road network classified by traffic function,
e.g., primary routes, secondary or distributor routes,
access routes, etc.;
(ii)   the present road network classified by road condition,
e.g., paved, unpaved, good condition, poor condition, and
bad condition;
(iii)  the present road network classified by indicative road
capacity, i.e. 2 lane, 4 lane divided, etc.
(iv)   distribution of intersections classified by
physical/traffic characteristics, e.g., at grade non-
signalized, at grade signalized; and
(v)    proposed additions or modifications to the existing road
network (including intersections, traffic signal systems,
street lighting, drainage, etc.) classified according to
status e.g. under study, study completed but without
financing, study completed with financing guaranteed, under
construction, etc. Where possible include Indicative cost
estimates and summaries of purpose for proposed
improvements (time horizons: next five year, next ten
years).
2.       Traffic Flow Characteristics:  from existing data, supplemented
where appropriate by limited surveys, prepare plans showing:
(i)    peak hour flows on the primary road network and at critical
intersections, and, where appropriate, those sections of
the secondary network with importanticritical flows;
indicate, using volume/capacity ratios, sections under
capacity, at-capacity, over-capacity;
(ii)   traffic speeds, peak hour, off peak, average during day
(primary network);
(iii)  journey times along principal links of primary road necwork
(if possible prepare isochrones from central area);
(iv)   peak hour delays (average) by location (intersection or
road section) on primary road network; where possible
indicate extent of delay (in minutes);
3.       Vehicle Operating Cost Data:  from existing data, supplemented
where necessary by limited surveys, prepare tables showing:



Attachment
- 127 -                    Page 2 of 4
(i)    basic unit cost data for gasoline (liter), oil (liter)
diesel (liter), spare parts (average per vehicle per
year/kilometers per year), tyres, etc. including a
breakdown of unit prices by financial cost, economic cost
and foreign exchange component.
(ii)   vehicle operating costs by vehicle type (private car, large
truck, microbus, bus, motorcycle); either by variation in
speed (if possible) e.g. 0 km/h (idling), to 10 km/h, 20
km/h, 40km/h, 60 km/h, 80 km/h, or by benchmark speed of
say 40 km/h; and by road condition (if possible roughness
factor cm/km). Note: vehicle operating costs would
include inter alia gasoline or diesel, oil, maintenance
(including labor, spare parts, tyres, etc.) and
depreciation and in the case of commercial vehicles (taxis,
trucks, buses) the wages of drivers, conductors, etc.;
4.       Provide information regarding the number of registered vehicles
and the growth rate.
Public Transport
5.       Route Structure:  from existing data, prepare plans showing:
(i)    the present bus 1  route network including bus terminals
and principal bus stop locations;
(ii)   present bus lines classified by "empresa", service offered,
frequency (peak, off peak), capacity (passenger seating
capacity) and loadings (passengers carried);
(iii)  areas more than 500 metres, and more than 1000 metres from
a bus route;
(iv)   sections of bus routes which suffer from delays because of
traffic congestion, poorly-designed intersections, bad road
condition, etc.; indicated average bus speeds for each
route section.
6.       Bus Fleet Characteristics:  from existing data prepare information
concerning the bus fleet including inter alia the composition, size, age,
capacity, availability, and ownership profiles of the fleet in the metro
area.
7.       Bus Ownership characteristics:  from existing data prepare
information concerning the "empresas" which operate buses in the metro area
including inter alia the number of empresas, the number or buses per
empresa, the staff per empresa and the ratio of staff per bus per
"empresa"; where possible, provide profiles of typical "empresas"
concerning their financial operations (costs of services, revenues from
fares and subsidies, borrowing capacity, etc.) and operating performance
(bus maintenance, out-shedding (proportion of their bus fleet which is
1/ Note: "bus" would also include other vehicles used for passenger
transport including taxis ("conchos") and three-wheel motorcycles.



Attachment
- 128 -                    Page 3 of 4
available for service and actually in service on an average day/week).
8.       Fare Structure:  from existing data prepare information concerning
fare structures including estimates of total receipts from fares, (per day,
or per week, or per month or per year) compared with total operating costs.
9.       Public Transport Proposals:  prepare information concerning
existing proposals for changes to the public transport system (changes to
the route structure, fares, fleet composition, size, age, capacity) and
proposed major investments in the public transport sector (bus terminals,
new systems of transport, etc.) with indications as to probability of
impler..entation (under consideration, under construction, financing being
negotiated, etc.) and estimates of likely costs.
Road Maintenance
10.      Road Mainterance Program:  from existing data prepare information
concerning current road maintenance programs in the urban area including
routine and preventive maintenance of road pavements, sidewalks, drains,
traffic control equipment (traffic signals, road signs, etc.).
11.      Road Maintenance Equipment:  prepare information concerning the
composition, age, size and capacity of road maintenance equipment
(including equipment for the maintenance of traffic control equipment, lane
markings and street lights).
12       maintenance Procedures, Staffing and Costs:  prepare information
concerning the procedures used for undertaking routine and preventive
maintenance programs (contracting to private firms, force account, etc.)
and indicate the costs of these programs in terms of staff, equipment and
materials, where agencies responsible for maintenance use their own staff,
indicate numbers and qualification of staff involved including their
employment status (permanent employees, contracted staff, etc.). How much
is budgeted for routine maintenance, how much for periodic, and how much
for rehabilitation.
Road Safety
13.      Accident Characteristics:  from existing data, prepare profiles of
accident characteristics in the metropolitan area if possible, showing
accidents by location, frequency and severity.
14.      Road Safety Programs:  describe current and proposed road safety
programs designed to avoid accidents. If possible, distinguish between
general educational programs, police enforcement programs and programs
concerning modifications to the road network and/or traffic control.
Institutional Development
15.      Agencies Responsible for Urban Transport Management:  describe the
agencies responsible for the following aspects of urban transport
management in the metropolitan area:



Attachment
- 129 -                    Page 4 of 4
(i)    traffic management and control (planning, design,
execution, supervision, monitoring and control of
improvements or changes to the road network, intersectiors,
traffic control devices, etc.);
(ii)   public transport facilities, services and o-erations
including improvements or changes in infrastructure (bus
lanes, etc.); route structure, frequencies of service,
levels of service, fare structure, distribution of bus
lines by "empresa"; changes in the number, size composition
and type of "empresas" providing bus services; licensing of
bus vehicles and bus operations;
(iii) the control, supervision and monitoring of public transport
operation and services and traffic flow and vehicles
(inspection, licensing, etc.);
(iv)   road maintenance programs including the collections of
accident data and the introduction of road safety measures
and programs.
16.      Azencies Responsible for the Allocation of Financial Resources for
Urban Transport Operation and Investment: describe the agencies
responsible for the financing of the urban transport sector including,
where possible, estimates of actual and budget expenditures for the recent
years available; describe the flow of funds to executing agencies and the
procedures adopted for the allocation of resources to the sector in general
and to the separate component parts of the urban transport system
(specifically traffic management and control, public transport, road
maintenance, road safety and administration).
17.      Agencies Responsible for Collecting Revenues Generate within the
Urban Transport Sector: specifically, the nature, extent and sources of
such revenues including the procedures for collection and subsequent
distribution to the relevant agencies.
18.      Manpower Resources in the Administration of the Urban Transport
Sector: describe, by agency, the number, qualifications and
responsibilities of staff involved in the management, design, operation,
control and monitoring of the component parts of the urban transport
system; where possible, provide organigrams of each agency indicating the
levels of responsibility, inter-relationships and procedures used.
